RATING: 9
I had a hard time choosing between 9 and 10 to rate this game. I reserve 10 for games like Chess, Go and Bridge. I went with 9. That said, BUY THIS GAME. OK, don't buy it if you think "Family Guy" should be censored out of existence.  CAH is rude, crude and thoroughly obnoxious. Don't play it with your priest/minister/rabbi unless you know ahead of time they like 4-letter words and bawdy jokes.

Do you already know Apples to Apples? It's basically the same game, but instead of being G-rated, this is more like R-rated.

Example: One player reads "____: kid tested, mother approved."  I had just picked up a card that read "The Female Orgasm."  I laughed and decided that it was just wrong for that and I played another card. However, I laughed and showed the card to a friend at the table. As he was reading it, the next host said: "____: you can't have just one." I took the card I was showing to my friend and slapped it down in front of the host. My friend said "if that doesn't win, I'll give you a dollar."  It won.

RATING: 3
I wouldn't define Cards Against Humanity really as a game. It is way to get to know the people you play with (or how confident they are with presenting really f***ed up answers to the group actually). What defines the description of a game even more is that the judge can use any arbitrary reason to pick the winner of a round.

So as a game I rate this a one. But as a past time party activity, I'll give this a three. There sure is some fun to the game and you have to think what kind of an answer the person being the judge that round will appreciate. However, even for this purpose you might not get any chance to play any funny combos if you happen to draw some really lame cards that nobody finds funny.

RATING: 2
Now I can say I played it, at least. It really is nothing more than an X-rated Apples to Apples, with a high quotient of cringe and gross. Good for some laughs as a social activity -- ours was a good group for that -- but as a game it left me flat. In time it got a little repetitive, and it stayed around too long to be enjoyable (which maybe would have been avoided if we bothered keeping score. We approached it as an activity, which was probably unwise).

Having played it once, I don't know how often I'd want to play it again, if at all (which also makes it similar to Apples to Apples in that regard). The first experience is probably as good as it's going to get: a good one-off laugh.

RATING: 1
I had the experience of playing this for the first time last weekend.  I'd heard a lot of good stuff; unfortunately what I experienced was less than awful.

The game is not funny, in the slightest, and gives players the authority to use otherwise socially and culturally unacceptable expressions within the confines of the game.  Its design is lazy and after 3 rounds, with 7 players (that's 21 black cards!) I didn't find even one the least bit funny.  Anyone who finds the statement "Batman's secret guilty pleasure is...Auschwitz," funny is lying, or simply effed.  The laughter was forced and the game overall awkward.

I'll leave you with this analogy: if players wouldn't write the punchline answers in games like Balderdash or Things, then there's probably something wrong with them (the cards) and it shouldn't be used as an excuse to seem 'edgy.'  It's just bullshit.

RATING: 4
How about a joke?

OK, what's the difference between a pile of bowling balls and a pile of dead babies?
Answer: The bowling balls are way harder to get into the back of your pickup truck with a pitchfork.

Funny huh? How about another joke?

So, what's the difference between a pile of bowling balls and a pile of dead babies?
Answer: The bowling balls are way harder to get into the back of your pickup truck with a pitchfork.

What, not funny anymore because you just heard it? OK, new joke!

What's the difference between a pile of bowling balls and a pile of dead babies?
Answer: The bowling balls are way harder to get into the back of your pickup truck with a pitchfork!

Now, if I were to repeat that same dead baby-joke one more time, you'd basically get the gist of playing Cards Against Humanity. 

Maybe I'll play along with it if I'm drunk, high or bored enough and I'm pretty much guaranteed of company is comically gifted enough to enhance the experience, but other than that this game really doesn't live up to all the hype.

I really don't like Cards Against Humanity.

RATING: 6
"A party game for horrible people." - this game really lives up to its name. The gameplay is very simple: you ask a question (black card) and then the others secretly select an answer from the white cards available in their hands. The the player who asked the question reveals the answers and chooses the one which he considers appropriate. The questions are nasty, the answers are nasty, so the fun factor is high with this one..

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Play begins with a judge, known as the "Card Czar", choosing a black question or fill-in-the-blank card from the top of the deck and showing it to all players. Each player holds a hand of ten white answer cards at the beginning of each round, and passes a card (sometimes two) to the Card Czar, face-down, representing their answer to the question on the card. The card czar determines which answer card(s) are funniest in the context of the question or fill-in-the-blank card. The player who submitted the chosen card(s) is given the question card to represent an "Awesome Point", and then the player to the left of the new Card Czar becomes the new Czar for the next round. Play continues until the players agree to stop, at which point the player with the most Awesome Points is the winner.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

Social lubricant score: 6-8 / 10 depending upon crowd and intoxication.

Gaming score: 4/10.

RATING: 1
As a rule I generally don't rate a game until I have played it half a dozen times or more but I had to make an exception in this case.

"Cards Against Humanity" is often hailed as being the answer to "dull party games" but I would argue otherwise. Humour is such an objective thing and so it should come as no surprise that some will find this game hilarious while others will not and instead find themselves trying hard to act like they found it funny. I am in the latter group.

The White Answer cards are stupid and are so on-the-nose when it comes to the shock value that it's actually pretty pathetic. Let me state clearly however that I am not easily offended and have no issue whatsoever with non-PC topics but I just found this to be contrived. 

There is no strategy whatsoever with the chosen answer usually being the most outrageous rather than the one that actually makes any sense. The game completely breaks down because of this as people choose answers like "The Queens immaculate anus" to questions like "How will we pay for things in the future?" - it doesn't make any sense! How can a uniquely singular item ever be used as a currency!? It is frustrating to see the Card Tsar pick a card that isn't yours (and makes sense) in favour of one that is just stupid.

I can't recommend this "game" at all. A far better party game that has options for creativity and filth, if you want it (rather than it being forced) is "Say Anything". Skip CAH - it's shite.

Here's a great rundown of why that's the case in my opinion:

https://www.shutupandsitdown.com/review-cards-against-humanity/

RATING: 3
This game attempts to take the hilarity of certain situations in "Apples to Apples" (the Helen Keller card comes to mind) and make a game out of entirely those types of interactions.

In Apples to Apples, the humor comes from people twisting an otherwise innocent set of cards. On their own, the cards don't do anything offensive. It's the player's sense of humor that makes it work.

In Cards Against Humanity, the sense of humor comes from the cards, and the player's personality and contribution is basically eliminated. You play the joke, you play the punchline, everyone laughs, you continue. The players contribute nothing; you may as well watch a stand-up comedian together. It's a worse (and less versatile) game because of this.

RATING: 2.9
If I'd only played this game once, it would rate about an 8. I actually gave it a 7 initially (after two plays) and the score has been revised down further since then.

Unfortunately, I find this game has far less longevity than similar games like Apples to Apples because the humour in CAH is often too blunt and feels pre-scripted.

There are certainly moments that have made me laugh but many of the cards feel too long-winded or specific; it's the cards themselves that are funny, rather than the clever way someone has chosen to pair cards together. A2A seems to have more room for variety in that regard; it's not necessarily as "funny" but when it is, it is so in much more surprising and witty ways because it allows room for the players' creativity.

Also the two-card questions in CAH tend to be more complicated and slow the flow of the game down too much. Not ideal for a party game unless you're only likely to play it a couple of times.

If you're after a good party game that will actually help you get to know your fellow players, I would instead recommend Apples to Apples (which also has a much larger number of cards), Say Anything or Dixit.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5.8
This is the adult version of Apples to Apples. One player reads a question then becomes the judge. Everyone else picks a card from their hand to get the judge to pick them as the best answer.

My big knock on this game is the lack of replay ability. Cards will end up repeating sooner then you think, and they become less and less funny with each time around. The first play through of this game is hilarious. The second is pretty entertaining. By the third you pretty much need the expansions to avoid duplication. There are only so many times you can laugh at the Harry Potter's b-hole card. Also it makes for judging to become skewed. Card A played to answer B might work perfectly in the judge's first game, but if it's the judge's seventh game then you've just wasted that comedic gold on a jaded judge. 

My recommendation is to play in moderation and keep the longevity of the game as much as possible. It's tougher to do then you think, because the first play through will be a blast and have you wanting to play it the next week. Avoid the temptation to keep the game fresh as long as possible!

RATING: 6.5
My friends and I will often laugh so hard we can't talk playing this, however be warned that this is a very adult and non-PC game.  There are terms that you will not want to have to explain to people what they mean.  Nothing, and I mean NOTHING is off limits in this game.  I'd give examples, but I am hesitant to on a public forum.  Everything from racist, sexist, raunchy, to flat out inappropriate (making light of atrocities) is par for the course.  Think apples to apples but for a horribly twisted sense of humor.

If you know someone that would be horribly offended by, well, just about ANYTHING, be careful playing this game with them involved.  You should most definitely not play this game with people in the group your doesn't know fairly well nor with co-workers.

My only criticism is that if you overplay this game (at like every get together you have) it will start to grow old.  The expansions will hold that off a good deal but, as with most things, overplay it and it will lose it's novelty (and shock factor!).

Look at my Wishlist for things I would trade for.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 2
The game's tagline says it all - it's a party game for horrible people. Specifically, Apples to Apples for horrible people.

Like A2A, this game loses its humor once you're familiar with the cards - people tend to laugh a lot more at anything card that's new and surprising. This is abundantly apparent whenever a group of CAH fans introduces a new expansion - you can watch as literally all of the laughs / points come from the new set.

The cards, obviously, will be offensive to some people while others will find them hilarious. If you're the type to find this hilarious, I can see why you'd be a much more devoted fan to this than A2A.

Mechanically, this game does have one advantage over A2A in the double-blank black cards. It doesn't sound like much, but being able to come up with different combinations of cards gives it a little more longevity.

Personally, I prefer games that require actual creativity over something like this. But weirdly, even though most of us in the hobby associate the lighter party game experiences like Why did the Chicken...?, Eat Poop You Cat, or even Attribute with non-gamers I've actually found the opposite to be true. My observation has routinely been that non-gamers often don't feel comfortable playing something that requires creativity or roleplaying in a group. That's the real secret behind the popularity of this game: it's for people who want to FEEL funny and creative but not exert the actual mental energy required to actually BE those things.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
I found the cards very funny and the un-pcness actually took me pleasantly by surprise. I'm glad a game like this exists. 

I think I would rank this game even higher since it is the absolute perfect game to pull out with certain people, but it does have a few issues. 

The game has very little replay value. I played back to back 4p games to 10 cards (~2.5 hours) and ran through nearly the entire base deck. There are 4 expansions that are almost required for any longevity, so this game is a significant investment. Seeing particular cards more than once (maybe twice) would definitely reduce the enjoyment the game produces, even if they are played on different subject cards.

The other issue I have, at least with the original, is the deck balance. After a few rounds, it is common to be left with a hand of somewhat boring cards for which there are very rare occasions where they can be used and be funny, so a few too many plays come down to just burning cards. I think the decks need some personal curation to maximize its potential for each specific group, but then someone has to see the cards and paritally ruin it for themselves to do this. Or you need to allow people to burn cards occasionally. Both of these solutions reduce replay value. 

All in all though, very few games are made that generate laughs at CAH frequency - the kind of belly laughs that only something so vile and wrong can produce. If you have friends who like that sort of thing, as I do, it is a perfect game for certain situations. 

Update: The expansions were disappointing to me. I felt the cards were not well-executed. And I have seen the game fail now. But still perfect for certain types so rating holds.

I have no strong feelings about this game.

It's more funny than most games that are primarily joke-delivery vehicles, but since most of those games are dreadfully un-funny, there's still some difference between CAH and the Algonquin Round Table.

The cards break down to roughly 35% puerile potty humor, 35% puerile potty humor that made me chuckle anyway, 15% weirdness for weirdness's sake that fell flat, and 15% genuinely incisive and funny jokes that made me laugh. Your mileage may etc. Good for a laugh amongst a group of like-minded consenting peers but I'd feel gypped if this ate into my actual gaming time.

RATING: 1
Apples to Apples with x-rated cards.  Look, I'm no fan of A2A, but at least you can occasionally try to have a clever answer.  This game just beats you over the head with it's politically incorrect and pornographic answers.
And no, my group and I are not repressed because we don't like this game.  We use much of the language contained on these cards, but we use that language while playing a game of Power Grid.  Because we feel like it, not because a card told us to.  It doesn't make us blush.

Finally, this game is dreadful for replayability.  "Oh, yeah, its the whole Glen Beck vomitting maggots card again...I'll go with pixilated bukake just because whoever played it probably doesn't know what it is."
You might be wondering why I have replayed a game I dislike so much.  The reason is that all my groups of non-gaming friends have individually discovered this and think it's the greatest thing since sliced bread.  If you found your way to this site, you should know better.

RATING: 6
An NC-17 version of Apples to Apples.  Leave your righteous indignation at home.

The one new thing it has going for it that really elevates the game is the concept of playing two cards per answer.  A lot of the cards require two fill in the blanks in order to make up the answer.

Instead of just throwing in your best card and hoping it beats everyone else's best card at the moment, you actually have to creatively think about pairing up two things that make sense.

I found these questions to be the most fun, adding a bit more strategy to the game and also cycling through your hand of cards much faster.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Pros: Easy to play, can accommodate many players, can be funny if you enjoy this type of humor

Cons: no depth, the cards get repetitive quickly, controversial and offensive humor

CaH is probably the most divisive game out there at the moment. On a personal level, I've enjoyed it. I've laughed and giggled and had fun with it in certain groups. If you're looking for a good party game for a group of people who will not be offended by the cards and have not experienced it, this will more than suffice.

The cards are unabashedly offensive, with no topic held sacred. Racism, sexism, genocide, and rape make an appearance. There is nothing wrong with being offended by a game with these topics in it; it is a completely valid criticism.

Outside the topics, the game itself gets rather stale, as  you move through the contents with blinding speed. The expansions do not add a particularly large amount of cards.

Cards Against Humanity is more an experience than a game. Experiences rarely have high replay value.

RATING: 7.4
I'd heard such good things about this game, I was anxious to try it.  And I have to say that much laughter should be illegal.  Our friend literally bruised her rib laughing so hard!

The base game is just Apples to Apples, but the cards themselves are a very WRONG sense of humor.  The type of humor that offends anyone and everyone equally.  So check your PC attitude and the door and sit down for a great time.

The downside here could be replayability. To help with that, the rules offer a number of small variants - we especially liked "Rando Cardrissian."  But these will only keep the game fresh for a bit - it becomes clear very soon that you'll want expansion cards.

RATING: 6
CARDS AGAINST HUMANITY

SUMMARY:
It's a dirty version of Apples to Apples.

PROS:
• A great party game. Many people who do not play board games will be at least somewhat familiar with Apples to Apples, and the rules are easy enough to pick up on.
• It's certainly a way to get people to break out of their shell in a group setting.
• There are a TON of expansions, and so this game has some replay-ability.
• This game always gets people talking and laughing. The fun of the game is in having the "Card Czar" read out all of the combinations, and it's always great to see them react to a particularly nasty combo.
• There are some interesting "House Rules" recommended in the manual that really improve the base game. The first is the Haiku, where all players produce a haiku from the cards in their hands at the end of the game. This is honestly the best part of the game, from the times I have played. The second is to add a dummy player "Rando Cardrissian", who plays a random card each turn... it is always funny when Rando ends up getting a point because his chaotic selection ends up being funnier than people who were actually trying.

CONS:
• The game gets exhausting after playing it a few times, so its shelf life is not very good without adding expansions.
• Cards Against Humanity is immensely popular, and lots of people like it. This shouldn't necessarily be a negative, but going along with the previous point... if you go to enough social gatherings you will end up playing this game many times, and you will become tired of it. Case-in-point, I do not own this game, and yet I have played it enough times at friends' houses that I am already "over" it. 
• The humor can be hit-or-miss. There are lots of cards that will do well in just about any situation, while others will not fair quite so well.

CONCLUSION:
• This is a fine game, for what it is. It relies a lot on crude humor, which can be funny the first few times, but after a few plays it will be time to pull out the expansions to keep the novelty fresh.
• The absolute BEST part about this game is setting up the "Pick 2" or "Pick 3" cards, and the haikus. It's cute to be able to match one black card up with one white card, but the rounds that involve putting multiple white cards together are when people can REALLY put their skills to the test for some great humor.
• For that reason it is a great shame that the majority of the gameplay revolves around matching only one white card to one black card.
• Ultimately, this is a fun party game that everyone seems to enjoy.

★★★★★★☆☆☆☆ 6/10

RATING: 4
First time playing this, I don't think I've ever laughed as hard in my life as I did that night.

Since then, I tend to either get bored, frustrated, or both. 

I know I should think of it more as a silly activity than a game, but I'm not aware of a more group-dependent experience. Lately, the best it has to offer for me is the occasional chuckle or appreciation of a witty combo. More often than not it's never having the right card to go with the question asked, or the frequent inability to tailor a response the person asking. It's at its worst when the group-think degenerates into an ever increasing escalation of who can play the most disgusting card, regardless of context.

RATING: 3
I don't understand everyone's obsession with this game. Sure, I go along with it when this is the only thing people want to do, but I don't like games that force you into dirty humor. I have no problem when that humor comes out naturally in a game, but this "game" (I consider it more of an activity) feels very artificial to me. I consider it an "activity" because most people I have played with don't end the game when a person has won a certain number of cards, but when everyone is tired of playing the game. I enjoy games that have satisfying and fun endings, not ones where people are tired of playing. I also don't the lack of creativity in this game. Sure, you can cleverly play a card based on some inside joke with a friend, but in the end you are restricted by the cards in your hand. "Say Anything" is a much better game in my opinion as it allows you to create answers...and if you want to throw in dirty humor, you're more than welcome.

Elke speler trekt 10 witte kaarten.
Eén speler speelt een zwarte kaart en leest de vraag luidop voor.
De andere spelers beantwoorden nu de vraag of vullen een woord in op de spaties door een gedekte kaart uit hun hand te spelen.
De speler die de vraag heeft voorgelezen, kiest het beste antwoord. Deze speler krijgt de zwarte kaart. Wie op het einde van het spel de meeste zwarte kaarten heeft, wint. Na deze ronde trekt iedereen bij tot 10 witte kaarten en wordt de volgende speler de lezer van de zwarte kaart. Soms moet je ook 2 kaarten uitspelen in een combinatie die je zelf kiest.

RATING: 1
The game really doesn't offer what I'm looking for in games. It's well and intelligently marketed, but I feel that the fundamental ideas shaping this game reflect the society that made it poorly. The game attempts to minimize agency to spread points (black cards) around evenly; it allows players to embrace the worst in stereotypes and uncomfortable humor, while trumpeting its own progressiveness for including cards like white people; its idea of a hilarious joke revolves around Batman. It's a perfectly designed party game, and I hate it.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 3
This is not a game - it is a box of cards that randomly creates someone else's jokes for you.  If you've been drinking heavily, occasionally the jokes are funny (but only the first time).  Most often, however, the jokes are so random as to be pointless.  I can easily make funnier jokes without this box of cards - and I would much rather spend my time doing this than playing CAH.

Cards Against Humanity is like the loud, crass drunk that you invited to the party because, for some reason, you thought he would be a fun time.  However, like all loud, crass drunks - 15 minutes after he arrives, the jokes stop being funny and you just want him to go home.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 4
This is less of a game and more of a social experience. There is no "game" here; no strategy and no thinking involved. You play it for the shock value and little else. Like many others have said, it is essentially Apples to Apples for adults.

The issue with Cards Against Humanity is how quickly it grows stale. After playing it a couple of times and cycling through the entire deck each time, I realized that the game rapidly becomes more mundane after each play. Not only that, but there are certain white response cards that will always get picked regardless of whether or not it makes sense with the black card. Where's the fun in that?

After finding that I would only play this for the enjoyment of others who have not played the game before, I immediately sold it. If you can find someone who owns it, is willing to play, and you have never played it before, go right ahead and play. If this is your type of game and you have a dark sense of humor, you will likely get some enjoyment out of this (especially while drinking).

However, is it worth owning a game that will sit on your shelf until someone new asks to play? Well, that's up to you.

"What is the woman's secret power?"
My answer: active listening
Winning answer: cum guzzling pac man.

...that's not a joke and it doesn't make sense??? But, because its the most offensive or raunchy it will win no matter what great card you play.

At this point I'd much rather play apples to apples. A to A is more versatile and allows for more creativity than its 6th grage cousin who's been held back about ten times.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
Even though this is just Apples to Apples, this is a perfect example of how humor can actually affect enjoyment. In Apples to Apples, you may get a few chuckles in the whole game.  Here, you are bursting with laughter on a vast majority of the cards.  The side affect of this laughter is twofold: 1. The judge is more likely to pick a better choice since the laughter generated is a great measurement, and 2. because you are laughing so much, you don't get annoyed at all when your card isn't picked. The pick two idea is also pretty cool, and allows you to be a bit more creative. The one downside is that you can quickly go through all the cards, which can take away some of the "shock humor" upon repeated plays.

RATING: 8
It's Apples to Apples except that the writers understood how everyone actually plays Apples to Apples. The first game is some of the most fun you'll ever have, just watching the reactions on people's faces as they draw cards and read things off.

Subsequent games are fun, in the same way Apples to Apples is, but eventually as you've seen all the cards the shock value that makes it shine during the first play is gone.

The thing that really makes it take off compared to Apples, is that you'll rarely be hanging onto cards because they don't fit with anything. There is a lot more freedom to make good combinations, and you're more likely to hold onto cards for the "perfect" combination rather than because you can't find a use for it.

RATING: 4
I enjoyed this game a lot, until I didn't. 

The core of this game is making offensive, rude, and dirty jokes. Which is fun! But the core of the humor is the shared understanding that the jokes are funny because some beliefs so ridiculous that nobody could possibly believe it. Or could they? When someone makes the joke that "no romantic evening is complete without roofies" is the joke "ha ha we all know nobody here is really this horrible, we just play at it" or is the joke "ha ha, I can't say anything like this seriously so I'll make a joke of it"? 

Somewhere out there, there are rapists playing this game and making jokes about how funny rape is, racists playing this game and making jokes about how inferior minorities are, and roomfuls of people happily laughing along with those jokes.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
I have Strong Opinions (TM) about Cards Against Humanity's ancestor, Apples to Apples. Much reviled in recent years, A2A has been largely replaced by CAH at modern millenials' gaming tables, as they've been drawn by its South-Park-like nihilism and built-in black humor.

CAH is good. Seriously. It works, for exactly the sort of group you'd expect it to work for. Most of the time you don't even need to be "clever" - just pick the grossest or most degenerate card in your hand and the judge will gleefully make his own associations.

With that in mind, though, here's my hot take on CAH vs. A2A: CAH, with its built-in jokes and laser focus on edgy, "offensive" humor, limits itself, making it LESS engaging for a creative mind than A2A itself!

In an effort to circumvent this, CAH's designers have created some alternative card types to the basic one-word adjective format that A2A relied upon. These new cards are like Mad Libs - short sentences with 2 or 3 blanks that allow you to add additional cards to your submission, in a particular order. This fails to work because 1. players can have a hard enough time finding one "clever" association that adding one or two more required cards increases the frequency of "dump plays" and 2. at a big table with a ton of people, playing a party game, people constantly fuck up the ordering rule, leading to frequent moments of "outing" themselves as they have to interrupt the judge to get them to rearrange the cards (spoiling the judging process), or else nonsensical and unintended word order. These cards also slow down the game, which is totally unnecessary in a party game like this.

People complain about the often innocuous card selection in A2A, but it's precisely that banal collection of words that forces the table to get creative.

CAH is still good fun, and its own brand of humor can really work with the right group, but I still contend that it's less satisfying to get a good card combination in it than it is in A2A. Half of the fun in A2A was to come up with jokes on the level of CAH in a game that was obviously never intended to support them! (See: "Colorful" + "The Challenger Explosion", a card combination I played once that I'll never forget, or "Loud & Clear" + "Helen Keller") With these combinations regularly coming out during A2A sessions, where is the need for a game like CAH? (The need stems from an absence of synonyms for semen in A2A's base set, I think.)
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 9
So, strangely, despite the silly/adult themes, this is actually a more solid game than Apples to Apples, the game it's basically ripping off.  It ends up being more fair and balanced, and not in the Fox News sort of way.  In Apples to Apples, it's rare to find a game where people are playing "correctly" the way it was designed to be played; the winner of each round tends to be just whoever happened to have the funniest card, or some other equally irrelevant criteria.  But in Cards Against Humanity, *everyone* has the funniest card.

RATING: 7
This is a kickstarter rehash of Apples to Apples with an adult twist. There isn't a whole lot of depth to gameplay, but it is highly entertaining with the right combination of cards and company.

If you feel that Apples to Apples gets monotonous with the seemingly demure answers, Cards Against Humanity is a refreshing change of pace. The adult humor revitalizes the game with its inherent obscenity.

If you don't want to shell out $25 for the base game, a [url=s3.amazonaws.com/cah/CAH_MainGame.pdf]printable file[/url] is available.

I'm very torn about this one. It can generate some very funny moments and even the awkwardness and nervous laughter can be enjoyable to a degree. But the cards themselves are very hit or miss. I love the ones that aren't inherently vulgar or attempting to be funny. The humor from the way things like "Miley Cyrus" "Black People" and "Grandma" get put into off-the-wall sentences can be very funny, almost reminiscent of the off-the-cuff answers people give on Family Feud or something. However, the desginers' attempts to be overly crass or make a joke on a card itself often fall flat with me. I think about 50% of the cards in this game could be thrown out and what was left would make for an enjoyable activity. Notice I don't say "game", because it surely is not that.

RATING: 1
Watch people playing this. They laugh at first, then as time goes on they laugh less. Eventually those laughs turn into embarrassed sniggers. And then silence. Yes, it is honest about how offensive it is but what it doesn't tell you is that you will abdicate your responsibility when playing it, you will become a bystander to the game and for me the whole point of playing games is that your choices are meaningful. You can be offensive playing apples to apples and create the same game, but it becomes your choice, using your brain. I know this opinion is not cool but I feel compelled to say it and I hope that this becomes an Emporer's new clothes situation where people actually think about what they are playing.

RATING: 5
(02/20/2016) Comment based on a handful of plays.

This is a silly, risqué card drafting game perfect for larger  parties, and certainly not for the feint of heart. "It's Apples to Apples for Adults." The questions and the corresponding answer cards suggest combinations that range from offensive, tasteless, crude, to just downright horrible. If the party is in the right frame of mind, this can be hysterical, especially if this is late at night. Eventually, the jokes run dry, requiring more expansions to keep the humor fresh. No matter what, the players are all going to burn in Gamer Hell. You will never feel "clean" ever again. :devil: Rating: "5".

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 1
I have never agreed with stalwart defenders of the "humor is the weapon of the oppressed" crowd. It strikes me as an easy way to excuse a lack of sincerity, and an unwillingness to seriously engage with difficult issues.

Thankfully, this game doesn't even have that defense to muster. It's pure vicious mockery, and a thinly veiled excuse for people to let their most disgusting opinions fly free with an easy cover of the cards making them do it. It's not funny, it's not entertaining, and it's mechanically boring and uninspired.

I get that CAH as a company have done some fun things, but I cannot get behind any company who has this pile of adolescent trash as their namesake product.

I try not to judge people by their taste in media anymore, but if you enjoy this game, I sincerely believe you should take some time to question why you enjoy it, and what that says about you.

RATING: 3
Yes, it was kind of funny to play. The FIRST time. 

Call me old-fashioned, but shock humor just doesn't cut it for me, especially when that's the only thing that something (in this case, a game) has going for it. 

I love a good dirty joke now and then, and black humor is right up my alley... but it's a seasoning. You have to sprinkle it and use it sparingly for it to maintain it's potency and effect. 

This game takes away the wit and creativity available in Apples to Apples, while maintaining the same frustrating card draw luck, and the same exact gameplay that does not age well. The one positive I found was the different judging cards (the combo cards, and more interesting questions vs. just an adjective). 

I've played it about 3 or 4 times and I'm just hoping people don't bring it out at any more social gatherings. PLEASE. Make it stop. 

Update: it hasn't stopped. But, I have found a way to have more fun with it: I play random cards from my hand without looking. In 3 games playing it this way, I've won twice, and was one card away from winning the third time. I do this to prove a point: there is no "playing" this game; it plays you. 

Update part 2: it still hasn't stopped. And it has only gotten worse.

RATING: 3
While it's popular in some circles to hate on Cards Against Humanity, my dislike of the game isn't due to any sort of "gamer elitism" or being a victim of having the game dominate game night and steal others away from trying new games (though I have seen that happen). It's that the game no longer stands out in the sea of Apples to Apples clones. It only has repetitive shock humor to offer and lacks the unique rule twists of newer games in the genre. It's boring, which is way more odious than being offensive.

Initial Rating: 5.0 (June 2013)

Ok game for a party game. Superior to Apples to Apples, but still too subjective to appeal to me (a judge decide which card won, at least each card is submitted anonymously). I’m going to sell it now (perhaps I will get it again later). The game made me laugh (which is the point) but I still prefer many party games over this one. Its main advantage is the grotesque/humorous/inappropriate theme. This is the best game of its class, most friends love it.

Lots of luck on this one, the player with the most curse, sexual cards will win. No strategy at all, just let it go and have fun. Perhaps a little pricey for what it offers.

I will play it if requested, however I don’t want to play it often.

RATING: 2
Concept is fun enough that I'd suggest everyone play it once with some close friends. And then never touch it again or you'll ruin the fun memories you could have made with the game.

There are all kind of problems... cards made just to offend, "OP cards" that simply always win, luck of the draw meaning that a dragged out game becomes less exciting (since you'll only have the sucky cards left), repeated answers/questions are just not as funny, etc.
But the biggest issue... the game doesn't make your friends funny. If you play a game like this, it would be awesome if the cards were simply guideposts, pushing your friends to make something cool with the stuff they're given. Players would be rewarded for presentation/execution, properly evaluating the judge's taste and adjusting their performance to suit those tastes, etc. CAH though... seems to do the exact opposite. Your friends become sideline characters, just means to deliver the cards on the board with their one punchline...

A totally un-politically correct game where a black card with a question, or a sentence with a blank space, is drawn by one of the players and the rest of them try to make the most funny, crazy or horrible answer possible in order to get awesome points, which are gifted by the player who drawn the black card.

If you play this game expect racial, religious or sex jokes (very explicit jokes), so this game is not recommended for people that can not handle that easily.

I don’t usually play party games, but I been enjoyed this one so far. I think it can get repetitive if you play with the same group many times, but the possible combinations are a lot, and part of the fun is to see people reactions, so bring new people to the game will refresh the experience for sure.

A card game which involves a judge choosing a black question or fill-in-the-blank card. Each player holds a hand of ten cards at the beginning of each round, and each player contributes card(s) to the "card czar" anonymously. The card czar determines which card(s) are funniest in the context of the question or fill-in-the-blank card.

RATING: 7.5
Type: Crass card-based, mildly competitive card game. Not for the prude!

Best With: 4-10
Weight: light
Duration: 60+ minutes (however long you want it)
Group Notes:
Raunchy card-based game.
About as easy and fun as it gets for an informal group game.

Cards Against Humanity is a card game best played with 5+ players. In each round, 1 player draws a card which has a question or blank in it. Each other player than plays a card from their hand of 10 cards that best (or worst!) fits that question or blank. The active player then reads the choices, and picks the one they like the best. The player who played that card gets a point, and the rounds repeat until someone passes the point threshold for winning.

This is a blast of a game to play. The answers are crazy, vulgar, disgusting...and absolutely hilarious. This is the sort of game that appeals to my dark sense of humor.

One downside to this game is the fact you do have to be careful that your gaming group can handle the subject matter of the cards. This is a game that appeals to people with a dark sense of humor and who know what things like queef, 2 girls 1 cup, and bukkake are (or who won't be turned off when the rest of the group explains them!). If you have people who will be too off-put by the subject matter, the game can become uncomfortable very quickly. Also, this game really can't be played in public areas.

Another downside is if you play this game too much and see all the cards, or most of them, this game does get a bit less interesting. Some of the best moments are when you see new cards you've not seen before being used in completely unexpected ways. But once you've seen all the cards, not many things will actually surprise you anymore. So playing this game should be done in moderation.

Similar games in my collection: Joking Hazard (raunchy punchline card game), Say Anything (free-form party game with many laughs), Star Fluxx (card-based fun, light game)

RATING: 4
"Assholes to Assholes" is a very apt description, but CAH improves on AtA's formula in a lot of ways. The Mad Libs-style cards are much more interesting, with two-element cards, haiku, and more to chew on. It produces a lot of laughter, often at things that are sick and wrong.

It does share my least favorite aspect of AtA, though: Having a bad hand the entire game and never getting any decent cards. I also wish there were more over-the-top offensive cards and fewer oddball normal cards -- more "Jerking off into a pool of children's tears," less "Batman."

Still: This is a lot of fun, eclipses AtA in every way, and makes for a great quick party game. I've never played it and NOT had fun.

---

I don't remember what rating this started at, but my guess is an 8 or a 9. I re-rated it to a 6 at some point, and now it's down to a 4. Most of the fun comes from "Haha, we're so inappropriate," but my hand of boring cards and the lack of actual game mechanics eclipse that pretty quickly.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
Cards Against Humanity is a card game that takes the Apples to Apples system and puts a perverse, misogynistic, racist, anti-religious theme on it.

On your turn you read a card from one deck.  The word on the card is usually some kind of adjective.  Then everyone else looks at their cards (taken from another deck) which are usually nouns, and hands one face down to the current player.  The player whose turn it is takes all the other players cards, shuffles them, reads them out to the group, then chooses the noun he thinks goes best with the adjective.  Whomever's card the person picked gets the adjective card.  Whoever has the most of these at the end of the game wins.

Cards Against Humanity's strength and weakness are the same thing, which is its ability to shock players with depraved word combinations.  It's a strength in the first couple plays, but with each new game the shock value decreases drastically.  However, even from the first play one quickly feels like they are being bludgeoned over the head with over-obvious teenage toilet humour.  It's ok once in a very long while, but that's it.  I would not recommend this game, at all though, if you are easily offended.  As the game produces a no-holds-barred attack against every group and institution.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6

Then I finally got to play this last month? this month?  and the first game was hilarious!  Everyone put in really funny cards, but somehow the cards I chose that I thought would fit the sentences, everyone thought was Rando hehe. Loved the first game and really wanted to play it again.  Was about to buy it also!!!!  Actually requested it hehe.

When the opportunity came around to play it again, I was mega excited.  Then I got dealt a hand with "gahhh!!" cards that there was no way I could read aloud.  Plus some of the religiously offensive cards came up that I hadn't expected since we didn't see them in the first game.  But being a Catholic I was a bit uncomfortable about the cards about our Saviour, and some of the racist cards.  

I'd still like to play it again only with the right people (which we had), but I think that I won't be buying and adding this into my collection.  I think I'm a little too conservative? naive? something or rather, to own this game.

RATING: 2
I'm told that this is like Apples to Apples...but with penis jokes and such. Which means nothing to me because I've never played Apples to Apples. I have played Cards Against Humanity, late at night, with a bunch of people who were at least one of the following: drunk, sleepy, confused or depressed. I was at least two of those (and I wasn't drunk), and it was an experience I shall not soon forget. Sadly, neither will anyone else on the same floor of the hotel, as a manager was none too pleased to inform us. Apparently, we (meaning everybody else, as I was trying to withdraw inside my own skull and ride it out) were not merely being too noisy--that would have been underachieving--but too noisy shouting things like "up the butt!" for reasons that I'm sure made sense at the time.

Don't pay any attention to people who say this is offensive. They have made the cardinal error of taking this game seriously. The proper amount of seriousness taking here should be slightly less than one nanomolecule (or whatever sciencey measuringey thing you use to weigh such trifles).

The game could be dumber, I suppose, and certainly more painful. I shudder to think exactly [i]how[/i]. Possibly it would involve the sudden, vomitous birthing of a tentacled monstrosity that, unbeknownst to you, had been incubating under your eyelid and was just waiting for an opportune moment to introduce itself. Whether this would make the game seem better in comparison I couldn't say, but some part of me fears it wouldn't. Mind you, I'm not volunteering to conduct the test. I've already [i]played [/i]Cards Against Humanity and therefore I feel I've suffered enough and am entitled to reasonable compensation, such as a half hour of naked cuddle time with a supermodel.

The true brilliance of this game is that it lives up to its name. I felt just a little less like a human being after playing it. So there's that.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
Think Apples-to-Apples, but for adults with darker humor. Players take turn flipping a black question/fill-in-the-blank card, and the other players choose a white noun/phrase card that they think best fits the black card. The player who flipped the black card chooses the white card that they like the best, and gives the black card to the player who played that white card. Random example: Black-"What's that sound?", White-"A mime having a stroke".

I. Love. It.

It takes what each and every Apples-to-Apples game eventually degenerates into (chosing the , and makes it the focus of this game. My roommates and I have played it so much in a short period of time.

It was a kickstarter success story, and it's typically sold on Amazon for about $25. Unfortunately, it's usually sold out (along with the expansion). However, the makers of the game will allow you to go to their website and just print out a copy of the base game (which is what I ended up doing).

I've listed it on my owned list and wishlist, as if I were to get the expansion, I'd probably want the non-DIY version with it.

LC- "Some combinations can be quite disturbing and graphic. Be warned..."

The first time you play Cards Against Humanity is likely the best time you played Cards Against Humanity.

I LOVE the humor. Every card feels like it was specifically engineered to get you to giggle. The people behind this game have a great sense of humor, even outside of the game. That being said... If your friends aren't funny, nothing will change that. Your unfunny friends might enjoy this game and think this makes them funny. It does not. The game loses its edge fast and hard and largely depends on the group you play with.

RATING: 3
As long as you go into this knowing what to expect, I guess it's not so bad: lots of potty humor, opportunities to toss around un-PC phrases, and so on...and I'm one of the "easily offended" people who takes issue with Archipelago and saying "niggardly."

My real issues are with the game mechanisms. Here again we have a Munchkin-like experience where you could glean most of the enjoyment of the game through just reading the cards. The game itself is simply an exercise in doing so. Unlike Apples to Apples, there are some cards that are clearly more ridiculous than others, and these will automatically win over a cleverly played pairing. To make this a better game, they could have taken out these cards, but clearly the design principles here were based the designers giggling and snorting "Oh my God, you [i]have[/i] to put that card in there!" rather than playtesting, restraint, balance, etc. As such, I can see this rating dropping a point with each subsequent play.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 3
This game appeals to the "I'm going to hell for this" type of humor enthusiast.  The basic idea is that the inherent cleverness of the joke is largely supplemented by the listener or viewer viewing the joke as inappropriate in other peoples eyes.  This works sort of similar to an inside joke, in which a lot of the enjoyment stems on the knowledge that not everyone will enjoy it.  The card combinations are all designed to set up something to be viewed as uncouth.    

"The US department of.....clitoris"
"Harry Potter and the chamber of...dead parents"

And such.  The idea to combine a silly idea with the image of other people being annoyed that you found humor in it.  

It fails in my opinion because EVERY damn card is specifically designed for the players to imagine it offending someone else.  It is 'shock' humor, just over and over and over.  If you are capable of pattern recognition, by the third turn you will start to get bored with dead babies and bestiality.  

In Apples to Apples, this sort of humor was possible, but just unlikely.  And I think if it comes out unexpectedly, something like this could be funny.  But when every card is geared toward making middle schoolers giggle, then it gets old fast.

-.5 crude humor can go down badly, risky game in mixed company.

RATING: 4
By definition this is a terrible game, but its sheer popularity alone shows that it must have [i]something[/i] that people seem to enjoy!

My main issue with CAH is that there's only a pseudo strategy for winning at best, and it is hardly a game at all in this regard. The key is to immediately order your hand from most to least shocking/offensive and then simply play best cards first regardless of context. This seems to usually get you a win pending other peoples' cards.

You can have a laugh over the random outcomes of pairing one card with another for a while, but I find it gets boring very quickly (even with a ton of the several dozen expansions that are now available).

'Yeah but its not about winning, its about making people laugh, but watch out- it could offend people!' The kind of people I hang around with crack way funnier and way harsher jokes then these cards every day. Seriously who gets offended by this 2nd rate South Park humour?

I'll never own it, and I'd never ask to play it, but I'm just willing to sit through it once in a while. In game terms its still a dog turd.

RATING: 7
[b]Like:[/b]
-Extreme simplicity
-No pressure for playing badly, you're only in the spotlight if you've won a round
-Some very funny words and sentences
-Somewhat known

[b]Dislike:[/b]
-Dangerous to hurt or offend someone (hasn't happened yet)
-Would not feel comfortable playing with everyone
-Would (probably) get repetitive fast

I never had a bad time playing it or someone who got offended, but I could definitely see it happen. Although I had some really great times with it, it is not something I would want in my collection; it would give people the wrong impression about the hobby and me.

While I could see this getting boring fast after multiple playthroughs (yes I get it now, "a big black dick" is funny with everything), since I almost never play it, the words still surprise me and as a result it hasn't been boring yet.

Monikers is the better game.

RATING: 7.5
4-30 players?  (I wouldn't want to play with more than 8, certainly.)  This is a "raunchier" version of Apples to Apples.  It's irreverent and hilarious, but I think some of the cards take the humour too far.  I played an 8 player game which took too long, so I would want to change the victory conditions for a large group in the future. Now that I own it, I have taken sandpaper to all the oppression-perpetuating cards (and some that just weren't funny) and written new things on them. It is much more fun this way, and I can play for more than an hour. Received the Jewish expansion for free; many of those cards had sandpaper taken to them. :P
My rating (7.5) is for my version. The regular one I might rate a 6.5.

RATING: 6
I hate Apples to Apples, mostly because I feel like there is no way to catch up if you fall behind.  In Cards Against Humanity this never feels like a problem, because so many of your card choices are awful and hilarious, and when you lose it's usually because someone else played something even funnier.  Fun game if you've got the right group for it.

EDIT: Big problem with this game - playing it too much, or letting a session go for too long.  If people stop giggling at the cards, it's time to play the haiku card and move on!  Fell way down in my rankings due to overplaying, and I'm not really sure I ever need to play it again.  It had its time in the sun for my group, and we've since moved on to things like Funemployed.

My opinion on this game pretty much mirrors the sentiment seen in Shut Up & Sit Down's review. 
All in all, I don't like it. I have had fun experiences with the game, but no thanks to the game. If I wanted a similar style of game, but with more to it as a game, along with a less crass tone, I'd play Snake Oil - which is a marvelous game!
I can think of no situation in which I would want to play Cards Against Humanity again. I've seen what it has to offer, and I've been left unimpressed - both with it's crass, edgy tone and with it's monotonous gameplay - and as a result of that, Cards Against Humanity is one of only three or four games that I've actively decided to remove from my library..!

Balderdash for Dummies. In theory, the game works well, but the whole thing seems to eschew any strategy or 'clever-jokes' for 'whoever draws the rudest card wins'. It's kind of arbitrary. RATING: 6
This game is quite simply Apples to Apples for people with a little more twisted humor. It isn't really groundbreaking in that sense, but it also doesn't lie about what it is. If you have the right kind of humor, you'll love this game. Tons of people give this game much lower scores and I've looked for a reason to dock points off this game. When it comes down to it, this game is a laugh riot and that's what really matters. It's always a good time playing Cards Against Humanity. It occasionally seems like we might have found all of the best combinations in the game, but then inevitably we get surprised with one of the funniest things we've ever heard. Plus with a good flow of expansions from Cards Against Humanity themselves and Crabs Adjust Humidity, the game can continue to be fresh.

RATING: 10
A fun and silly game, not for everyone due to the humour, but it can be a lot of fun if the crowd you're playing with is up for it. It can even be played as a 2-player game, with a third imaginary player being operated by the current Card Czar totally at random. You'd be surprised at just how funny random answers can be.

The game does not scale as well as it claims. Anything above 8 players gets mind-numbing; hearing 2 or 4 or 8 potential punchlines to the same joke setup is one thing, but having to wade through 10 or more ceases to be funny. I recommend playing as teams when you have a crowd of more than 8 people.

RATING: 4
Obwohl ich mittlerweile keine Lust mehr auf Cards Against Humanity habe, sind mir die Erinnerungen an die ersten Partien voller Lacher durchaus noch viel wert.
Gerade für Leute, denen Brettspiele eher fremd sind oder solche, die ungerne auf Druck kreativ sein möchten, kann CAH Abende voller Lach-Bauchkrämpfe bescheren.

Nur ist der Witz irgendwann erzählt und das übrig bleibende Spiel bietet weder Platz für Eigeninitiative noch Cleverness. Wie ein altes Witzebuch, bei dem man eine magere Pointe nach der nächsten vorliest.

[u]Gute Alternativ-Spiele:[/u]
• [b][thing=8829]Nobody Is Perfect[/thing][/b]
Behält das Frage-und-Antwort-Schema von CAH bei, bietet jedoch die Möglichkeit, mit Halb- oder Unwissen den Mitspielern urkomische vermeintliche Begriffsdefinitionen als wahr zu verkaufen.
• [b][thing=158564]Billionaire Banshee[/thing][/b]
Hier ist wie bei CAH zwar auch keine Kreativität gefragt, dafür bieten die lustigen, fiktiven Lebensabschnittsgefährten viele Gelegenheiten, um in Gespräche über ideale Partner abzutauchen und dadurch oft Möglichkeiten, seine Mitspieler in "Beziehungssachen" näher kennenzulernen.
• [b][thing=46213]Stille Post Extrem[/thing][/b]
Auch hier ist keine eigene Kreativität vonnöten - dafür wird gezeichnet. Und je weniger man dies kann, desto lustiger wird die Runde häufig.
• [b][thing=178570]Die Unüblichen Verdächtigen[/thing][/b]
Wenn die politisch inkorrekten Witze der reizende Faktor bei CAH waren, könnte DUV gut passen. Hier tanzt man mutig auf einer Schlängellinie zwischen Vorurteilen, Humor, Rassismus, Menschenkenntnis und Selbstreflektion.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
There's a great controversy about this game. Some people feel offended by it and some others think it's ultra-mega-fun. I'm in the middle. I'm not easily offended and certainly not by this game, but there are some things that even if they don't offend me, they doesn't seem funny to me.

In fact, the main idea about finding word combinations is great and it is supposed to provide loads of fun. But then I don't find the execution that funny. People tend to give points to the most outrageous and sexual fill-in cards, no matter if they don't make sense at all with the main card. And that's the part I don't like. You are supposed to make funny combinations. I can see myself laughing at a joke about dead babies, but it needs to be funny. A random sentence about dead babies won't make me laugh.

You could say that the game is not to blame about it, that it is the behavior of the players. But that's not totally true either. The game includes deliberately provocative cards that promote this behavior. 

So, overall, for me it's a story of what could have been.

A couple of additional random thoughts:
-> I guess it has a low replay value, especially if it's played this way. The jokes will quickly become old. Fortunately, you have plenty of expansions for that.
-> It's dangerous to play it with strangers. It will improve when played with people you feel comfortable with.

RATING: 1
To be clear here, I don't actually have a problem with the "theme" which seems to be mostly the problem for a lot of people that don't like this. 

I simply don't get the appeal of it. The game is all about giving "funny" answers, but giving funny answers to me is not funny at all when it's the game that is already giving them itself. You simply pick one from a limited choice and that's it. There is no creativity, no insider jokes, just picking one you happen to have. 

To me Say Anything (which for me eventually is also just an "ok" party game) does exactly the same thing when you play it with fun people, but as the answers are not just read from cards but actually made up, it can be actually funny.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
An excellent party game for the right crowd. And I mean you really need to know if your friends/family are ready for a game like this. This game is dirty! The game box says this game is for horrible people. It is not for the easily offended or even the somewhat offended. It is likely that everyone will be offended by some card or other in this game. This also is not a game to play with students. For all you teachers out there that like to provide a game day for your students...do not try this one. Also, don't let your students convince you that you need to play this game with them.

Now after that big disclaimer, it is without a doubt well play tested and hilarious party game. This is essentially Apples to Apples in it's rules, but with some differences I mention below. It amazes me as to how many diverse answers to the questions fit so well and in so many unusual/funny ways. If you want to just play with 2 players and a dummy player it is fun and works. This is unique to this party game, because most are absolutely unplayable with 2 people. 

The dummy player is essential to any game, because you will want to blame a really bad card on someone else and a dummy player really is funny. Some good dummy player suggestions are (Yoda, your cat, a family or friend that isn't currently playing the game). We use a squeeze toy named Happy that laughs hysterically. 

Another awesome feature to the game is the wager you can place in any game turn. If you have won a card, you may wager that card allowing you to add a second card to the selection handed over to the judge. If you win a card that round you keep your wager and the won card. If you lose that round the wagered card goes to the winner of the round.

Not very high for replayability after a few sessions, but with the right people and a bottle of vodka? A great game with lots of laughs.

RATING: 8
This kills off Apples to Apples for me. The change from just nouns to having all sorts of matching requirements (Blankety-Blank questions, situations, multi-answers, and so on) provides a lot more opportunity for cleverness and laughter in the answers. And the provided answer cards are more interesting to read and choose between as well. Adding a general layer of smuttiness accelerates the laughs, no matter what you think. Having a fun, easily taught game that can play quickly and take a high (and variable) number of people is an asset to a collection.

RATING: 4
Whilst a blast on purchase, several years down the line and I've given this game away. More than 4 players slowed the game down significantly.

Also every round was reduced to most offensive card wins and/or rounds of rubbish answers where all players were just discarding cards from their hands which was about 50% of the time.

Whilat constant expansion purchases would have negated some of the issues perhaps I just didn't want to keep buying new decks. 

For a similar and somewhat more rewarding experience try Cyanide & Happiness' comic strip game. Or just play codenames. Not (as) offensive but very fun with large groups and massive replay value right out of the box.

RATING: 8.1
This game combines two of my personal favorite things: 1. Being creative 2. Being humorous. My friends told me that this game was "created for people like me." The only two things I don't like about it are: 1. Some of the cards just feel like they shouldn't be in there. Some of the proper nouns especially, where no one at the table knows who the person or thing is, and the joke is lost. It's always frustrating. And 2. You really need at least 6 players for this to be any fun, which can be a challenge at times. My favorite games tend to be ones that are most fun with 3-4 players. HOWEVER, as long as no one at the table is easily offended, this is a great game where everyone will most likely be laughing while you play and that is always fun.

It is a rare case when one can observe a game in passing and know exactly how it plays. This was the case with CaH. I'd seen it played at cons and hearing just a few of the punchlines, I pretty much knew how I felt about it. My one play confirmed it. It was great for a few laughs as long as players are comfortable saying terrible things around one another. The owner of the game couldn't (or wouldn't) tell me how long it was supposed to last ("we usually play until we've gone through all the cards"), but I was ready to be done well before that happened. I think 2 or 3 times aronud the table would be appropriate. This will get stale after hearing the jokes a few times, so I'm glad to play once in a while, but not own Cards Against Humanity.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
This is a word association game that's essentially an Apples to Apples clone only here the cards are focused on being strange, dirty or offensive. The early plays of this game were hilarious for the shock value effect. As the game got played more times, and the shock value wore off, we started using the cards to more and more creative effect. I still enjoy the game in theory, although I've shyed away from short filler games lately in general. I'd still play this over Apples to Apples, because I feel there are fewer cards that wind up as duds, although in the case of both games, as you mix in expansions, it pays to go back and remove some of the cards that don't work well with your group.

:nostar: Art, Iconography and components functional
:nostar: Clever or interesting mechanisms
:star: Reasonably low downtime between turns with mildly AP players
:star: Multiple plays stay interesting
:star: Low or mitigatable luck elements
:star::star::star::nostar::nostar: Raw enjoyment

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 1
As we call it around our house, "Assholes to Assholes." 

I've laughed at every John Waters movie; I've read every issue of Paul Krassner's "The Realist" I could get my hands on; I think Gilbert Gottfried's take on "The Aristocrats" is hilarious; Peter Cook and Dudley Moore improvising as Derek and Clive makes me laugh like a drain. Those are all examples of vulgarity and bad taste by very creative people. This game is just vulgarity and bad taste for amateurs. It commits the cardinal sin of comedy -- almost every single joke punches DOWN. 

Some perfectly lovely people I know just adore this game, and if it gives them a few cathartic belly laughs, I see a reason for it to exist. I don't hold the fans of this game in contempt, but anybody who gives up after a hand or two gets an extra serving of my respect.

SEE:

http://www.shutupandsitdown.com/blog/post/review-cards-against-humanity/

RATING: 4.5
What I would like this game to be is absurd, what it ended up being with the people I played with is a bit too obvious and literal with the connections. There are certain answers that are just more extreme than others and will be chosen almost no matter what question they are paired with. 

I liked trying to come up with very unexpected combinations of question and answer, that start to make sense if you just think a little bit about it, and then it is really funny. But those answers are rarely chosen. I guess it's because I have a Marx Brothers humor in a Three Stooges world. Apparently, my friends just think I'm pretentious.

This can be a fun party game and I like it better than the first time I played it. For me there are some cards that shouldn't be in there. The game works for me when it goes for blasphemy and doesn't try to offend for the sake of being non-PC. Maybe it would be different for different people which cards cross the line. And I would suggest everyone just taking those cards out and not playing with them.

The cards get old pretty fast, after about 4 plays you probably get through most of them and the more extreme answer cards stand out more and more. I would say either rotate through new cards or new players pretty frequently.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 4
Essentially the "dirty" version of Apples to Apples, and improves on that game, but not by much.  I actually prefer the mechanics here; I think filling in the blank works better than simply associating adjectives and nouns, and they even spice up the formula with things like double blanks and haiku.  

The more risque approach also makes this a lot funnier than Apples to Apples, but watch whom you play with; there are not only some filthy cards but some that could be disturbing or seen as pushing the line (such as the 9/11 or V-Tech Massacre cards).  

The problem with this game is the same as with Apples to Apples:  the formula gets old rather quickly, and once the shock value and novelty laughs wear off, those same outrageous cards just aren't as funny anymore.  

You need a couple expansions to keep the cards fresh, but even so, this game works best as a one-time opener with a new group.  Break the ice, get everyone laughing and loose, and then move on to other games.  If, like Apples to Apples, you play it all night or many gaming nights in a row, you WILL get sick of it.  There's only so many times you can laugh at the same poop joke, after all.

RATING: 7.5
A more adult version of Apples to Apples. Very funny, especially the first time you play. After a while you start seeing the same cards, which reduces the funny unless you're playing with different people each time. Several cards are deliciously offensive, so avoid this if you have reverence for anything. Also note that while Apples to Apples you are charged with picking the card that MATCHES the best, no such rule is here. Your job here is to simply pick your FAVORITE. On the one hand this alleviates a frustration I have Apples to Apples:  irritating players who pick their favorite card instead of recognizing a good match. On the other hand, I've seen players who are trying to win Cards Against Humanity also get frustrated by the card czar skipping over your (great match) card for arbitrary personal reasons. It's best to play this just for fun. Also, I highly recommend you play with the Rando Cardrissian variant, as it encourages players not to overthink it. The variant also makes a 3 player game quite playable.

RATING: 8
I liked playing Apples to Apples a lot but I always felt it lacked by not having any raunchy cards. So naturally, when I finally got Cards Against Humanity I was really excited, but after several play-throughs I find that I almost become desensitized to it and the funny cards become less of a surprise. I also find that I am consistently holding out for cards such as "Toni Morrison's Vagina" or "AIDS" or "Menstrual Rage" as some cards are pretty much an instant win. My boyfriend and I both enjoy poking fun at the Twilight Saga, so one day we picked up a copy of Twilight the board game at savers and stole about 40 cards from that and we use those very often in cards against humanity. Depending on the group, sometimes the Twilight variant packs a harder punch than the original game itself. Overall, a great game, easy to play, and it always guaranteed a few laughs.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6.2
Components - 1/1 Card Stock is fine. Instructions are straight forward.

Fun - .7/1 Honestly my wife and I are horrible people, and we have a bunch of horrible friends. This game is hilarious in those situations. We've had our fair share of entertaining combinations, difficult decisions, and pants wetting laughter. At the same time, like Apples to Apples, with the wrong people (e.g. Decent human beings) this can easily become awkward.

Replayability - .9/1 Large number of cards and since it's all about the combinations, you can play over and over again and still get new experiences. The only reason this isn't perfect is because the best combinations tend to be the most offensive, when playing for a long while (or repeated nights) it can feel a little samey even though the cards are different.

Strategic - .5/1 A large part of the game is what is in your hand versus what card is played. There's a little playing the meta by picking a card based on the reader. Unlike Apples to Apples though, you generally have more than a single choice in your hand that could work.

Theme - .1/1 "A party game for horrible people". That's what they advertise it as, and that's what most of the cards represent. I give it a partial point for that. Otherwise there really isn't a theme.


Personal Review - 3/5 I think this is a great party game/filler. It's what Apples to Apples should have been. There's enough cards that most plays have cleaver answers and the decider actually has a choice. Generally you as a player have more than an obvious choice for the category. It works. Then again, if you get offended by things, then this definitely isn't the game for you. We tend to enjoy it because we're probably horrible people.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
This game is basically a vulgar Apples to Apples.  The game includes black cards that have questions or fill in the blank sentences on them and white cards that include mostly vulgar and awful responses to the black cards.  The reader each turn picks his favorite answer that the players turned in and that player gets a point.

As long as you have friends who are in this game's target audience of "horrible people" this can be great, hilarious fun.

We like to play with the Rando Cardrissian variant where we put a random answer in every turn as well.  If a random draw from the deck turns out to be funnier than everyone else at the table's answer then you should feel bad!

Even with the huge number of cards available (I even have all the expansions) this game can get kind of stale after enough plays.  There's only so many hilarious answers you can come up with before the shock value wears off and they all start to sound same-y.

RATING: 4
Can, at times, generate real, genuine laughter, but often becomes repetitive and most players of CAH don't go for the more clever card combinations. The description "Lego for jokes" is the nail in the coffin-- lots of other games can be much funnier thanks to the efforts of the players, and in fact Lego allows for much more creative expression than this. In CAH, literally any group of experienced players I've played will at times preface their black cards with "If you play X card, you win" because the jokes are so obviously constructed. It creates shock humor that fails to be shocking, because it is so artificial. It has been a passable icebreaker with certain groups of people, but if I could replace it entirely with another game, I happily would.

RATING: 1
I hate Apples to Apples, but I despise Cards Against Humanity.  I think it is because for years it was the "hip" "naughty" game to play, so everyone had to bring it over and insisted on playing it like it was the rebellious thing to do.  The first few times are good, the next several aren't.  Additionally it gets really embarrassing and uncomfortable for everyone when a player asks what something is.

Perhaps my biggest complaint about voting games is that often times the stupidest combinations win.  I can't tell you how many times I have played this and thrown away cards win the round.

If you want to do a matching game pick one of the others out there, but even then don't ask me to play.  I hate these voting kiss-up games.

P.S. The reason this is a 1 is because this game isn't innovative, it just copies games like apples to apples and adds NSFW elements.  Furthermore, it has no design and nothing but black and white print.  I would go sofar as to say the cards are worth nothing more than the energy contained within them for a fire.

RATING: 5
Apples to Apples for bad people.  Tons of laughs the first time while drunk but the game gets really stale rapidly after.  It's just not a good game, but it does serve a purpose.  It exists solely for non-gamers, the unfunny and dumb people to perform an activity which mimics the trappings of a game.  Sadly it's become most peoples introduction to card and boardgames despite it's awful nature.  If you fancy yourself remotely funny or intelligent choose something like Snake Oil instead.  This is just not a good game, it gets points for entertaining morons who feel a little naughty for stringing together reprehensible things which can break the ice at a party.  It's pretty much the gaming equivalent of 13 year old boys looking up dirty words in a dictionary and it does what it does well enough.  In some ways it's depressing in it's very existence, All you need to do to be successful is steal the mechanics from another game and write poop jokes on the cards.

RATING: 1
OSHA mandates the inclusion of handrails for a game with this much edge. Completely dead for anyone who was good at being funny in their teenage years. It's not that the material is offensive; it's just that I've already thoroughly plumbed its depths and these punchlines will be in their refractory period for the foreseeable future.

CAH's veritable army of [-]fluffers[/-] [-]strap-ons[/-] expansions, first-party and otherwise, do little to assist its attempts to simulate youthful vigor. Its only redeeming quality is that it's better at teasing larger non-gaming crowds, where offering up an actual game -- one with, say, proper rules and a victory condition -- would require too much explanation and not draw enough people. It would be a better use of time to rewatch [i]The Aristocrats[/i]; this stuff isn't even amateur hour.

I'd originally ranked this more forgivingly -- "not actually a game" is a rather harsh judgment to make just based on distaste -- but in this case it's actually true! Cards Against Humanity isn't a game; it's a read-through of a script full of uninspired dirty jokes. Even the Penis Game (the one where you try to yell "PENIS!" the loudest in a public space) is better, as it 1: costs less, 2: is funnier, and 3: has winners and losers and an end condition!

RATING: 4.4
It’s not that I get offended easily when it comes to playing this. It’s just that it is, to me, all about trying to get cheap laughs via vulgarity. I’ll always favour a tactical game over a party game, but if I am to play a party game, I’ll at least want it to be either 
A) challenging on a tactical level;
B) challenging on a trivial level; 
C) challenging on a dexterity level;
In theory if a party game offers one of these, it should be fun. Cards Against Humanity doesn’t. My friend Dree summarised it well when I asked him what he thought of it, “It’s not intelligent enough for you!”
