RATING: 7
It's an adults Apples to Apples. Better when drunk, for pretty obvious reasons. You have to be comfortable in yourself and in your friends in being a horrible person who is going to play things that just bring up terrible, terrible images.

But with the right group of people, this game brings lots of laughs and a ton of fun. 

I don't rate it higher than a 7 because a) there's really no end condition. You pretty much play until you're tired of playing; and b) there's a couple of house rules that need to be implemented - for example, exchanging cards - or you end up with a fist full of cards that you are just looking for opportunities to throw away.

All in all, we've played twice, and it's a pretty solid game.

RATING: 9
Burns bright, fades fast.

Ive enjoyed hundreds of games of CAH over the years, but after the first 20 or so it became harder to enjoy without adding more expansions. I've purchased every expansion and promo they've sold directly since release, and it seems like each expansion tends to add another 5-10 fresh plays before it gets stale again.

By nature, the shock wears off, and at a certain point you've conceived every combination of horrible things you could create... That's when it gets dull.

I would definitely still recommend this for adult gaming groups, but I feel that the developers would be better served by crafting some way to tweak or modify the core gameplay in their next expansion.

Some new gameplay mechanics would go so much further than another 60 pop culture reference cards.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
How this game is not rated higher, I just don't understand. This one has always been a huge success for me with multiple groups of friends and coworkers. Maybe I'm just a horrible person and know too many horrible people?

Yes, it's the same game as Apples to Apples just with a sick and twisted personality, but it's that personality that makes it so entertaining. This game is intentionally outright vulgar and (to some) offensive, but it works hard to do so, with a good bit of intelligence, in the way a good shock comic should be. The inventiveness of the cards alone shows that being a horrible person takes a lot of creativity. Then it's what you do with those cards. To paraphrase a favorite holiday movie, some people work in profanity the way other artists might work in oils or clay... it is their true medium! Check out some of these for examples:

http://www.hexjam.com/uk/news/funniest-best-cards-against-humanity-answers

https://www.buzzfeed.com/hnigatu/hilarious-awkward-rounds-of-cards-against-humanity?utm_term=.hiVRMwGVJ#.ciDOzqvd6

So, this is more than just the NC17 version of a PG13 movie... if Apples to Apples is Will Smith, CAH is Eminem; if Apples to Apples is King of the Hill, CAH is Rick & Morty. It's a George Lucas blockbuster... directed by Quinton Tarantino and co-written by Louie CK. This game has a personality and a character to it... a delightfully deranged one that believes no topic is off limits if it might bring a laugh.

I truly enjoyed (and still do with groups that I don't think could handle the content and subject matter of CAH) the basic idea of Apples to Apples, but Cards Against Humanity takes the best parts of that game and jumps way over the line with it, into a world of dark, twisted, sick, and outright explicit humor. 

It just doesn't get old, and one of the few games I have where the game play experience improves in direct proportion to the amount of alcohol consumed by the players. In fact, it's amazing how a game like this and a few drinks can turn even the most reserved and well-mannered seemingly stand-up citizens and pillars of the community into a vulgar, licentious, macabre-loving sickos.

So, leave Apples to Apples for playing at Thanksgiving with that Aunt who would become outright offended and indignant, but play CAH with interesting people with thick skins and over-active senses of humor.

RATING: 3
I was excited in getting to know [thing=50381][/thing], mainly due to the laughs I heard while I was, two times, near a table in which the game was being played. And there was several of these moments in my play. However, I did found out that [thing=50381][/thing] isn't really a game, is and activity - if we were telling fishing stories, or throwing water baloons at each others, the result would be mostly the same, only probably more wet. That is because the "game" doesn't demand any type of consistency in the subject proposed by the reader - in fact, is the other way around, as there more your answer have nothing to do with the subject, better are your chances of being selected, due to the surprise, absurdity and chock effect. Also, the decision of the winning answer is 100% subjective. It is almost like that in [thing=18723][/thing], but, in this, the guilty of the round makes more sense, the one that twisted the answer the worst and the one that couldn't pass the guilty to other; still, the chosen can be picked by the Dark Overlord without any discernible reason. I did it because I could. [thing=50381][/thing] is like this, but all the time. Pretty lame for a game. The laughs are also, several times, traded for confusion and embarrassment (as when someone tells a bad joke), provoking wry smiles, as the people at the table can't understand the connection of the subject and the answer, nor even enough to laugh, because there is the amusing [i]non-sense[/i] and the plain and pure [i]non-sense[/i].

There was, as I mentioned, fun moments (the best, for me, was when the question was something like "When I got high __________ turned into ______"; and the winning answer was "When I got high 72 virgins turned into Stálin". Luckly I wasn't drinking at the time, as I laugh hard); but there is no doubt that, if were we doing thumb fights or bowling, there would also be plenty of laughs.

[thing=50381][/thing] has an expected social element - playing at random could produce results (maybe not winning, but one could probably have several cards picked, and I have seen people not all that adjusted to the game "mood" that playing randomly would probably improve their chances), but one most likely will fare better if you know what sort of person you are giving your answer to, at least remembering what sort of logic he/she applies in choosing the card: some will like gore, others movie references, others more "behaved" answers or more connected to what was proposed. This won't be a sure thing, but can help.

Still, the most outlandish answer, regardless analysis, can only go so far. Several times someone at the table had "the perfect answer" and not once I saw one of those being chosen. Therefore, you can only hope to hit a nerve, to strike a chord, in order to win rounds.

Now, is this a "game" about winning? No, of course. It a pastime, to entertain. But here I wanted to analyse the "game". It is indeed a game (without quotations) in the sense that hide and seek or a drinking game is.

For casual play, I'm in. Not something I willing to play on regular basis.

RATING: 6
Every complaint people make about Cards Against Humanity is on the mark. It substitutes creativity for canned responses. It mistakes shock value for comedy. It loses a replay value quickly. New players are the best way to keep the replay value up, but they also choose the most obvious combinations. I don't care about any of these complaints. It's just a bit of immature fun. However, Paul and Quinns at Sit Up And Shut Down recently made a point that I can't overlook. They claim this game is only funny to those with perfect lives. As an ethics instructor, I know the statistics on child abuse. With a one in seven chance that someone will be forced to laugh to cover up their own trauma, I fear further victimizing someone less fortunate than me. Ditto for other cards such as as those about dead babies. I'll have to do some thinking about how to address this.

RATING: 6.5
Good:
-Hilarious and creatively vulgar cards
-Hearing people actually read cards/combinations
-People laugh when they read a card for the first time

Bad:
-Too offensive for some
-Players often reuse the same pairings and are disappointed when it doesn't get the same laughs
-Not as funny when you've seen all of the cards a few times
-Tired, played-out format

Overall:
You get your money's worth and it will seem like the greatest game in the world during your first few plays.  After that, you tend to only want to play with people who haven't played before as the hilarious becomes predictable quickly.  With that said, hearing someone unable to read a card without laughing or cracking up after drawing a card makes it worth bringing to the table.

RATING: 3
It's a very popular game and many of my friends and family own it. Therefore I played it already numerous of times even though I never personally bought the game. What I can say is that it was fun for a bit, but then it got boring and eventually it got extremely bad. Making things sound reasonable is rare in this game and profanity just isn't that insanely funny, especially after seeing the same cards frequently.

Maybe the game isn't great because it's just words and plain colors, or maybe there is just way too many sentences on these cards for scenarios to turn out good. I'm not sure. However what I can say that this game might be more amusing for people who like a random, incoherent, disgusting, profanity based games. Might be great for teenagers, but very lacking for adults, and this game is also definitely not for children.

Now I wasn't by any means offended by anything nor do I dislike profanity, but this game for it to work, requires some structure to make a hilarious outcome. I've very rarely saw any. I've also played the game so much to tell you that the replayability is VERY low. Once you seen all the black cards, you felt like you've seen everything. Now you must be thinking that maybe I just didn't go through all the expansions. However I did and there is more that keep coming. It's the same thing though, you go through all the black cards and then you don't want to play again.

Chances are that I might play again because my family and friends did buy the cards and will most likely want to play, but now with Joking Hazard released, this game will soon be out of the picture. Fun while it lasted, even if it was just a bit.

RATING: 4
After a few plays and listening to others, for me personally I don't perceive much long-term appeal. Cards' chief power is in seeing newcomers' reactions to reading cards for the first time as they combine the implications of their combinations in their head. That's fine and it is truly funny, but ultimately quite limited.

There is also for me a strong point on which I'm willing to stand: that some things should be treated with delicacy. Making a joke about rape might not make me feel uncomfortable, but if it makes someone in my group feel uncomfortable, furthermore, to the degree that they don't feel able to speak up about how they feel due to the general consensus that it should be funny, I'm failing in my responsibilities as an ambassador of this culture. Make no mistake, it's not all about me - it's about the people we commune and share time with, and I will affirm and defend that to the highest degree. You might be able to joke about abuse with your mates, fine, but don't assume that everyone is on that train, especially people you don't know, and you *are* accountable for them - for your behaviour when you're around them. It's just as easy to not joke about rape and abuse so just don't do it.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 2.5
An important part of this type of game is that the cards are balanced so that people don't just pick a card because it made them laugh. Apples to Apples is, in my experience, a better game when you remove the "Helen Keller" card because people look at the association between the red and green cards, rather than just picking the card that made them laugh.

CAH, of course, ignores this because they want every card to be shocking and funny to read. But it's just not possible for them all to be equally funny, so the game devolves into "who played the funniest card" with no cleverness at all.

Combine this with the fact that that type of humor is honestly pretty shallow, especially if taken all at once over a few hours, and this game really bums me out.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
